## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and driving terms. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or coupling between variables.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear friction)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-varying stiffness)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v**2 + c2 * v (velocity-position coupling)
- General quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v + c3 * x * v (all quadratic terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry x→-x
- Even-power terms in x (x²) → asymmetric potential, breaking left-right symmetry of oscillations
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → energy dissipation or injection (damping/driving)
- Products of x² and v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillators (van der Pol type)
- Explicit trigonometric dependence on t → externally driven oscillator with periodic forcing
- Absence of explicit t dependence → autonomous system where energy is determined by initial conditions
- Cubic position term x³ with same/opposite sign as linear term → hardening/softening spring nonlinearity
- Odd powers of v (v, v³) in damping → symmetric damping under time reversal, common in physical systems

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v` = `0.7675*sin(t) - 0.2639*v*sin(x)`.

The GT has two terms:
1. `F0*sin(t)` - a sine function of t only
2. `-beta*v*sin(x)` - a product of v and sin(x)

The key challenge is the `v*sin(x)` term. No simple combination of `v*cos(ct)`, `v*x`, `v`, etc. can reproduce `v*sin(x)` since sin(x) is a nonlinear function of x that doesn't depend on t.

Let me check candidates that might produce a `v*sin(x)` term or equivalent:

**Candidates with exp(c*x) terms (like candidates 2, 11, 23, 41, 42, 43):**
These have `exp(c4*x)*sin(...)` which can't become `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidates with cos/sin(exp(x)) terms (1, 7, 10, 26-28, 36, 38-40, 49):**
These have `cos(c3*t + c4*exp(c5*x))`. If c5=0, then exp(0)=1, and this becomes `cos(c3*t + c4)`, just a function of t. Can't produce v*sin(x).

**Candidates with log(|x|) terms (8, 47, 48):**
These have `sin(c3*t + c4*log(c5*|x|+1) + c6)`. This can't separate into sin(t) + v*sin(x).

**Candidates with x*sin/cos terms (3, 5, 12-20, 22, 50):**
These produce terms like `x*sin(...)` or `x*cos(...)`, not `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidate 25 and 31:** These have rational expressions with `1/(c1+x²)`. Let me check 25 more carefully:
If c1=0, terms become like `c0/x`, `c2*sin()/x²`, `c5*v*cos()/x²`, `c7*sin()`, `c8*v*cos()`, `c9*v³`. Still can't produce v*sin(x).

**Candidate 34:** `c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*v*cos(c4*t)`. This gives sin(t) + v*cos(t) type terms, not v*sin(x).

**Candidates 44, 45, 46:** Simple sums of sin/cos of t and v terms. Can't produce v*sin(x).

**Candidate 2:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*exp(c4*x)*sin(c5*t+c6) + c7*v*sin(c8*t+c9)`
Could `c3*exp(c4*x)*sin(c5*t+c6)` become sin(x)? No, exp is fundamentally different from sin.
Could `c7*v*sin(c8*t+c9)` become `v*sin(x)`? No, it's a function of t, not x.

**Candidate 9:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*v*cos(c4*t) + c5*cos(c6*sin(c7*t+c8))`
The third term is a function of t only. None produce v*sin(x).

**Candidate 21:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*v*cos(c4*t) + c5*exp(c6*sin(c7*t+c8))`
All terms are functions of t (and v), none involve x through sin(x).

None of the candidates contain a term that can produce `v*sin(x)`. The term `v*sin(x)` requires a product of v with a sinusoidal function of x. Looking through all 50 candidates:

- Terms with x appear as: `x*cos(...)`, `x*sin(...)`, `v*x`, `v*x*cos(t)`, `v²*x`, `x/(1+x²)`, `log(|x|+1)`, `exp(cx)`, `x²*...` — none of these are `v*sin(x)`.
- No candidate has `sin(x)` as a standalone factor multiplied by v.

The function sin(x) cannot be represented by any polynomial in x, exponential in x, logarithm of x, or x times trigonometric functions of t.
